Ok so got me a bunch of acrylic sheets and have been wanting to do the Narc from Alien for a while now. Just scored one of the terrible Aliens jobs, yeah i know they are different models with different angles etc but i want it for comparrison. The Alien Narc will be a complete scratch and if i can nail all the donors will be accurate to the studio model. I got pretty much all the available refs out there but to start with i could use some help with the interior. so far the obvious 8 rads stick out but i haven't really been looking through any kit scans so any help would be greatly appreciated.

Re: NARCISSUS Part id help

DERRRR it's R2. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 That's not the only Star Wars kit you gonna need either, LOL. 

You are gonna need a lot of the staples. Two Centurions, two 1/12 Tyrells, the Scammell, a Revell Gemini, that Airfix Superfort and way more 232s than you think. A whole bunch of trucks and truck trailers, not the regular ones though. 

I had the complete list from Martin, but I paid a pretty penny for it and it's embargoed. Still, I can't really stop you from having a gander at my Narcissus stash shelf next time you're over! I seem to recall he did publish it himself on his site at one point, anyway. I had a look just now in case it is still there, but couldn't find it. 

In the meantime, drawings; should be a start. Crosscheck the dims yourself, don't take mine as gospel.

[IMAGE: narcissus-part-id-help-narcissus-v0a.jpg-99599d1340546251]

OK so listing off what we know from existing IDs, photos of the original and from MB's replica builds:

Tamiya Centurion 1/25 x 2

Tamiya Tyrell 1/12 x 2

Tamiya Tyrell 1/20 x 1

Airfix Vosper MTB x 2

Airfix Esso Tanker x 2

Tamiya 1/35 M16

Tamiya 1/35 Schwere x a stupid number

Tamiya 1/35 Leichter x another stupid number

Revell Gemini (just the pilot)

Martin tells us there are 27 kits needed, so that leaves 18 kits to find.

Yeh man, there's several mistakes people make commonly with this ship. Most common one one is to make the front half too short overall. Next most common is to give it a dip between the front upper hull and the nose. It is almost dead flat in profile.

Post #58  (forum post #2330122)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Jun 27, 2012 at 5:03 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: NARCISSUS Part id help

Me too. The windows are different because the whole front hull is a little shorter and differently proportioned. Even if you are the guy who originally built something, you're not going to copy it perfectly 30 years later unless you have the luxury of indefinite amounts of research time. Martin is a working pro and doesn't have that luxury, so "95% accurate and built by the original guy" has to be good enough.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: NARCISSUS Part id help

Ok .... So I've had a few Pm's input Kitting this model. If I do the plan will be to provide a few options. One will be all the acrylic laser cut pieces of the main body. It will have the styrene panels pre cut on a sheet so you can just pop them out and stick em on and finally the resin kitparts bagged into their separate areas ie rear top starboard panel etc.

The second option wi be to provide the files and you get your own bits cut and I provide the resin parts. Much cheaper to ship but you'll have to source the cutting yourself.

Not sure at this stage but I will start an interest thread in the JY when the time comes.

Thanks.... Simon.

Post #259  (forum post #2460293)
Author    : JD1
Date      : Sep 7, 2012 at 5:21 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: NARCISSUS Part id help

Pretty sure that small hatch is from the 223. It's sand-coloured in the pre-paint workbench pic. The 'rectangle with bottom corners missing', left of the four Centurion 'hinges', is also 223, B7.

The tiny round part in the corner to the left of the lone Scammel ramp is 232, but may not be on the original, as it's also sand-coloured.

The panel Martin's used under the '351970' marking is from the Panzer Kampfwagen IV, but again may not be studio-correct. It just looks a slightly different shape and length on the original.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #260  (forum post #2460320)
Author    : JD1
Date      : Sep 7, 2012 at 5:40 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: NARCISSUS Part id help

Not sure those four identical Centurion parts are kosher, either. Once again they're sand-coloured on the original, where the only Centurion sprues I've seen are grey, dark green, and black.

I think Centurion part E12 is on there, in the section just above the cut-out for the aluminium turning.

Post #323  (forum post #2482811)
Author    : Rats
Date      : Sep 19, 2012 at 11:24 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Also, the yellow marking to the right of the palm tree is a TAC marking indicating a towed artillery unit. The Hanomag has similar decals, but not in yellow (at least not in the newer issues). It is not specific to the Afrika Korps.

Cheers, JT

Post #330  (forum post #2486934)
Author    : emojo5
Date      : Sep 22, 2012 at 7:46 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

The symbols that have the circle with the cross thru them are what we use to call "Registration Marks". I used them earlier in my design years to create mechanicals. They register an overlay acetate sheet to a mech board. 

They were made by Letraset (as well as Chartpak) and came on sheets as well as on a roll. I might even still have an old roll somewhere. Love this thread and would love to hear about how I can get on the list for this kit. Thanks.

Oh yes, they also had a reversed version (if I remember correctly) for use on black boards. That's the other type of reg mark used in the glove photo.

-emojo5/Ed M

Post #454  (forum post #2511182)
Author    : jedimaster
Date      : Oct 5, 2012 at 5:53 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Cheers Niels... I must say it has been a fun group build so far (no fights) and the common goal of bringing everyone the most accurate Alien Narc has gone very smoothly. Almost organic in nature. An important factor I think is that there are no Ego's in this build just a common love for this model.

For me I think it was born out of Necessity. I think it was Frank who started a thread here somewhere asking what Ss models we would like to see that hadn't been done as yet. The Narc was always on the top of my list as was the turbo laser. So if I can't buy it I'm just gonna have to build it. We really did have a leg up on this with Martin Bowers "list" and his build and of course it helped that Martyn (Nwerke) also had a bee in his bonnet over this model some years ago and started his own research. Paul has turned out to be a bloody legend. I asked him some time ago if he wouldn't mind drawing me up some basic DXF files of the hull shape and well... Trust an engineer... We now have this beautiful structure we see today. Crossed referenced all known refs and Martyns drawings which were already pretty damn close I might add.

Then there's Lee with his skill at id'ing and drawing up the decals. It really has been a group effort including Fred and all those who have contributed refs. I think realistically we should start shipping kits in January. Once I have the weight of the cut acrylic we may offer a full kit shipped but that's all up in the air at the mo. If not it's the files resin and decals.

Thanks everyone for the work so far..... Now let's get this puppy (piggy) finished.

Simon.

Post #516  (forum post #2515016)

Date      : Oct 8, 2012 at 8:49 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

No worries mate off to find one now. So I figured out a L'il issue I was having. Paul printed me off the 1:1 styrene panel templates and I was matching kitparts against those and comming up short. Even with the correct trimmed parts. Now if this was the case then our model was too small by about 5 mm. Turns out the templates were off and not the model. Now that could be the printer that was used or our Genius got it wrong but the main thing is the models dims are just fine. Been messing around with some kitparts.

/9B570EDC-5074-4D83-9701-15272AC4D1C7-125-00000113C5038

Post #529  (forum post #2516381)

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Ok... So we had a Board Meeting and came to the unanimous decision as for the cost of the files. The Files will set you back a mere $300. For that you will get all the Dxf files required to build the Narcissus. That includes the 3mm acrylic and the 1mm Styrene panels. You will also receive assembly instructions. This  will be paid directly to Paul (Woodlake). There is also plans to build your own armature. Either in acrylic as Paul has done or Steel/aluminum as I have. If you want to get cracking on it straight away these should be available next week. So if you are collecting your own kitparts the wait won't be long. If you are waiting on the resin parts then at least you'll be ready when they arrive. I will post here when they are ready and update the interest thread in the JY.

Thanks

Dudes, I have a concern about the location of those conical drum details on the stern, and in turn about the overall length of the 'tails' that they sit on, and the nozzles.

I know they're definitely not correctly shown on my old side view, but in trying to pin this down I'm finding parallax is an issue in every single one of the reference shots. Some make it look like the drums are fully forward of the end of the nozzles, others like they're fully aft of that point. (If that were correct, we'd need to stretch the acrylic 'tail' parts).

My guesstimate is that it's likely the centre line of these drums which is in line with the tips of the nozzles. Agree/disagree?

Jason, ha ha, yes and no. I still differ on a couple few things - Martin's nozzles are basically square in elevation whereas mine taper more; the overall height of my engine is slightly greater, as is the cross-sectional area - rivet-counter stuff like that. But I was definitely wrong to think his engines were substantially (10mm or more) shorter than they should be. 

Craig, damn right - if God had meant man to work with poly meshes he would have given us computers for brains or something. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 :lol

I have three small styrene prototypes in my shed and one abandoned SS armature, so it's not as fast as all that if the original research counts, ha ha. Just kidding, I never got anywhere with it and all credit to Paul and Simon as this really is moving pretty quick. Speaking of, we just wrapped up a morning meeting here at my place, we think we have ways forward on a few questions that had arisen. 

We'll be making some changes to the engine seat areas in particular and have a few more plans on how to tackle this or that. Man, that proto looks good in person!

Post #615  (forum post #2525684)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Oct 13, 2012 at 9:36 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

:facepalm having some mesh errors appearing on the uploads. Bit of rework.......okay, done. I didn't actually get it in the print queue last night - PC crashed just as the final upload was at 97%, which I took as a sign to go the **** to sleep.

I tried a single-part upload with the nozzle included but it is likely going to be easier to mould as a separate part and slightly cheaper to print that way anyway for some reason. Anyway, HAVE now hit 'print' and should have these in hand in a couple of weeks (now I'll find the rest of the errors, lol.)

Jason, heh! The final part will be hollow though probably not as thin as this (2.5mm wall thickness); might need to clay it a little for casting. It's mainly about saving moolah TBH, since Shapeways charges by the cubic centimetre. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Clamp part also in print queue now. Paul - thanks for that file - I added in the whole structure. I just looked at it and thought 'this might as well be one piece'. It's a deviation from fidelity admittedly, soif we don't like it when we take a look, we can always just cut the extra bits off. 

Oh also I redid the strake detail on the nozzle, I'd thinned them down too much. Gone back to thicker strakes, looks better IMO. Old version and new version shown here. Nozzle-less body too, to show that that looks like on its own.

I'm still unsure - it could be shadows, couldn't it? But I've always wondered how the clamp was supposed to work practically, and trimming this part might easily have been a solution to some fit problem. I propose we provide the part complete, and builders can trim it themselves if they wish. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Wolvster, the reasons number three, three being the number of the count - to five shalt thou not count: 1) I'll likely second-guess myself on the exact location for the lines anyway, 2) it's easy - I have two thirds of bugger all skill in CG modeling so five minutes with a pencil and scriber will equal four hours of struggle in Rhino, and 3) we're using real kit parts for the side details, I decided to use real Evergreen too, might as well use real panel lines, heh.

Five. Three, sire! <lobs holy hand grenade>

BTW - anyone have a clue what Evergreen part number to look for for the ribbed panels? I don't know their range at all, never used it in fact.

She just kept relentlessly trying to fob me off with generalities and refused to put me through to a supervisor - I got one eventually but had to ask forcefully several times. I'm a mild-mannered nerd, I'm almost never an ugly customer, but I went to 11 this time and for once I didn't feel ashamed to do it. 

Orrrrhhh, um, polyethylene? Soapy and slippery type? Right swine to glue and paint if so but we'll see. If no go then I am pretty sure I've got some 3'x6' styrene sheets in the shed - I shoulda saved you the bother - soz!!!

Yeah, Simon gave me the 3/16 figure and I scaled it into the drawing I'm using; it looks about right. You could also make 7/32 work but it's an odd size, hard to find and a little on the big side. 

The next common size down would be 1/8 and that's definitely too small IMO, so I think we're good. Different diam on some of the others though. Also the intersections are complex - look closely guys - Simon, they're not simple cuts, have you noticed?

Post #666  (forum post #2539797)
Author    : Woodlake
Date      : Oct 21, 2012 at 5:12 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

My original plan was to use .75mm styrene for the paneling pieces. However my plastic supplier had none in stock and would have to order it in. He did however have some other .75mm plastic, and seeing as though it would be painted (and it was dirt cheap!) I thought I'd go with it. 

As the paneling details are so intricate, my cnc router was not really an option. I had the idea of fitting a pen to the cnc and using it as essentially a large plotter to draw the pieces out onto the styrene. I even built a little pen holder from scrap perspex..

[IMAGE: attachment.php]

The stuff I ended up with is clear/bluish, so it was just easier to trace the printout of the layouts directly on it. I didn't even get to try it out! :rolleyes

[IMAGE: attachment.php]

Although Martyn and I have made various tweaks to the plans, the majority of the panelling layout remains unchanged. 

This exersise hopes to confirm that everything fits as it should. 

So far, so good. 

I'll let the pictures speak for themselves...

[IMAGE: attachment.php]

[IMAGE: attachment.php]

[IMAGE: attachment.php]

[IMAGE: attachment.php]

[IMAGE: attachment.php]

[IMAGE: attachment.php]

[IMAGE: attachment.php]

Still lots to do - stay tuned....

Sure but then you gotta pay them also which drives up the price. A member here has shown interest in laser cutting the pieces for the folks in the states. As soon as the finished files are ready he will look at them and make his decision as to if and how much he will do them for. Now if I ship 20 resin kits to him with 20 armatures that is gonna cost me a packet and he then has to box up and send again onto you. He ain't gonna do that for free. So when I get everything together, I'll have a better idea of shipping. If your happy with that I'll send a you a complete kit. If not you will receive the resin, armature and plaque etc from me and the acrylic from them.

The kit will be reasonably priced..... But I'll let you decide when the time comes. Some will no doubt drop from the interest list as the price may not suit them. At the moment this is an RPF Exclusive... Once orders are filled here I will offer it on other forums. No money will be taken until the order is ready to ship.

Simon, honestly, keeping it metric is fine with me, if that counts for anything (LOL). I prefer using metric because ten-base is logical... damn Imperial system, lol. ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Finished off the nose by gluing the nostrils in place and adding the sytrene:

[IMAGE: attachment.php]

I though it might be a good idea for those folks that will be adding the cockpit or lighting option to be able to remove the main top panels for access. To achieve this I have added a couple of extra pieces of acrylic that allow the top panels to be fitted togther as a separate unit. To this I then added 2 rare earth magnet at the front and 2 to the rear, with corresponding magnets glued to the ship. Seems to work well...

[IMAGE: attachment.php]

[IMAGE: attachment.php]

For the rest of the weekend I have been progressing on the styrene layout for the top of the ship. Still lots to go, but here are some progress shots...

[IMAGE: attachment.php]

[IMAGE: attachment.php]

Ouch, bummer, Paul! Model looking good.

I just sealed up and posted the upper engines. They're on Shapeways now, now if only I had some money to order them with! Fun budget is spent for this fortnight, waah. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Referendum: having spent a LOT of time poring over pics of the original model, I no longer think the 'scoops' are scoops. On Mr. Bower's replica engines they are recessed front and rear, but on the original, photos are not conclusive - but seem to suggest they're just solid blocks. The engines were cast in fibreglass - the replicas are too, but my suspicion is that the production versions were simpler. 

I could easily include intakes front and rear, but for now I've made them solid. Opinions, preferences...Bueller?

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

With thanks to Martyn, I now have a set of the beta version of the 3D printed lower engines and wing clamps (both of which have since been modified for their final incarnation).

The engines have not yet been fixed into position, but for the clamps I added a "plug" on the back which is a push fit into the armature frame. 

This allows their removal at anytime and the option of mounting the model from the side.

[IMAGE: attachment.php]

The other additions to the ship over the weekend are the pieces that are on the top and run down the top panel to the nose, as well as the 4 trim pieces that run along the edge of the ship from back to front.

This just leaves the rear half of the ship and the central front panel styrene layouts to be finished off.

Post #829  (forum post #2608392)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Nov 27, 2012 at 8:10 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Great stuff guys. Hey I basically wrapped up the new lower engines last night. Will post a render tonight but I have a couple of questions for the peeps. 

Are there two vertical panel lines on the sides of the main lower engine body, or just one? There's one in *every* pic, but some pics show a second line further forward. Maybe a pencil line, or added late? 

Secondly, if that line exists is it the one across the very front of the engine - right at the point where it's 'cut off' on that angle to form the seat for the Leichter hull? Or is it separate to that? I just can't decide.

I mean, obviously if it is in any pics then it was on the model at some point, but I can't work out why it would be missing in the blu-ray screencaps, which seems to be the case.

On the other hand, have we discussed any more about how weird those caps are WRT decals? I don't think it's a case of anything falling off the model; I think it could be deliberate intervention. There are very faint pinkish smears where there should be, for example, a large red text placard decal, or a big red arrow. 

Did someone on the BR release decide the model was overcooked on the decals front and digitally mess with them?
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #830  (forum post #2608902)
Author    : Lee S
Date      : Nov 28, 2012 at 2:27 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

From what I can see there only ONE line that goes all the way down the side.  I've looked at every pic I have and they all show the same as this:

All sizes | Narc_02c | Flickr - Photo Sharing!

Even that doesn't appear to show the rear panel line, but others do.

As for decals! I've been staring at them for months!  The front and back are very different.  The back is mostly based on the full size set and the front a 'regular' miniature.  As the fullsize set only had tiny decals, they couldn't/didn't put on on the back.  I don't think it's because of the BR or that they were changed after.

Also remember that decals were ADDED during production, look at the shots of the garage door being slid back and then of it being lowered.  There's more decals later...
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Got the new nozzles, clamp and upper engines last night. I say 'clamp', singular, because the other one was missing. Only one of the two new nozzles is good; the other has a kind of rubbish surface finish; doesn't appear to have been grown at the same time.

Both engines are incredibly rezzy, much worse than the two lower engines. Looks like they grew them on their sides for some stupid reason, instead of longitudinally. Only one panel line came out perfectly, the others are absent or faint. They are usable but will need a lot of elbow grease first. 

My worst ever Shapeways results, I have to say. Have had a wee whinge about that!

Post #862  (forum post #2624315)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Dec 5, 2012 at 5:42 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Bigturc, yes. These are way the worst results I've had in a ton of Shapeways orders this year. See also http://www.therpf.com/f10/narcissus-builders-club-n-stuff-151894/index30.html#post2558853

It's the orientation in the build tray that is the problem. When you make a flattened domed dish-shaped part then it has to be grown in a flat orientation and you're going to get that topographical map effect, it's a limitation of the process. 

But with these engines they can be grown from the nozzle base up in a vertical orientation, giving much much better control over the surface - as with the lower engines Paul posted. It's disappointing they grew these horizontally....especially on their sides! - since it guaranteed "wood grain" on both sides. 

If they won't fix those then that's okay, I can clean them up as they're big enough to work with. The one good/one bad nozzles are kinda irksome though; they're for moulding and part of the POINT of all this is that stuff should be identical! :lol
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #870  (forum post #2635357)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Dec 11, 2012 at 11:41 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Got a refund from Shapeways for the nozzles and missing clamp. Nothing on the wooden engines but oh well, I didn't insist on that. A lot of models get built at once; their orientation can't be chosen by the buyer.

The factory picks whatever will be cheapest, so if you don't get a bunch of other people buying 'tall' models at the same time, your model will be built 'flat', and you're out of luck. Better stock up on sandable primer.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Ok.. So I just got the first one in from my plastics co. I'm gonna pop out the pieces tonight and box it up. Should have shipping quotes tomorrow and final prices. The panels are on a sheet of .75 clear PVC. It's the same stuff Paul used for the proto so we know it works. We may change this to hips later. We have cut it to the maximum of .5 so you will just have to get the exacto and a steel rule and the groove should guide your blade nicely and this stuff is easy to cut. Sorry for the bad iPhone pix. More tomorrow.

Click to expand...

The "dogleg" will be the cause. Any internal corner will have to be squared out (there are only a couple from memory). This is inherent with using a round router bit at internal corners. Even so 1mm - 1.5mm won't create any problems. 

I'll might add a note to the instructions to cover the issue...
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #934  (forum post #2707164)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Jan 22, 2013 at 8:58 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Yep. I got it right with the cutouts for the armature, but I know I went wrong with the shoulders. I was just surprised I went as wrong as that - I did square it out, but one side had a cleaner cut than the other. I squared to the wrong mark, in other words.

Speaking of the armature, it's a super tight fit. The dims are accurate - it IS a fit, but a lot of wiggling is needed. I wouldn't leave the metal armature in direct sunlight or really hot weather with the acrylic parts fitted up, in case of expansion. 

(Which is what I have now done of course; let's see what happens. Taking one for the team since 1967...) :lol

BTW I am enjoying working with the acrylic. THERE is something I never thought I would say, I usually hate the stuff. But this build is very enjoyable - parts snap out easily, there's little cleanup, and the assembly is rapid.

I used the acrylic armature for mine, so expansion is not really a problem in that case.. If it's too tight a fit, I would give it a light sanding to loosen it slightly. Its not critical that it be that tight because once everything is fixed together it is very solid and wont move anyway.

Click to expand...

Hey Martyn,

The parts list I have shown in the instructions is not representative of the sheets layout as supplied from the plastic manufacturer. They were provide a single file with all the parts and they then arranged/nested the parts themselves to best suit the sheet size. 

The parts shown in the instructions are just grouped into areas for ease of reference.

You should not have triple of T1 or T2 though, and T4 should definitely have a hole. I have checked the file I exported for them and everything looks correct this end..

It may pay for you to go through all your parts and just compare them to the parts list in the instructions to confirm what you do and dont have.

I still have some scrap acrylic here. If you need some of the missing pieces cut (rather than doing it by hand), just let me know.

You will need to take the protective sheet off to see if any damage has occured. I thought I might have a few scratched here and there on mine, but the protective layer does a pretty good job, so you may be lucky. If its damage from the router, we will have to let them know to use a higher clearance plane for future copies to avoid the problem. 

Really the only area of concern is the windows as everything else is covered and sanded/painted. It'd be sods law if your windows are affected!

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

J if I had known you were waiting on the armature I could have sent that part out. I'll cut one up this weekend. We had to tab the acrylic for CNC as the table is a vacuum bed. The more surface area you cut out the less suction to hold the sheet in place so you run the risk of the sheet moving during cutting. Wouldn't be a problem on the laser though. Just means a little more clean up for the builder but nothing to worry about. The price difference here was $400 for laser cutting so we went CNC.

Martyn glad the engines fit. No more revisions required. Good news. You and I just need to cast up the parts, me to finish the cockpit and sort out the files with the plastics guy and were almost there. There's a few parts I haven't id'd as yet , not many but I need to sit down and go through my kits again. I started to go Sprue Blind.( yes it's a condition we all get at some point.) If I can get p/ bucket working I'll post some pix of the parts I need later today.

Quick question re the hatch insert for Paul. The floor of it is well below the 'scale' floor line; any particular reason for that or am I missing something obvious? Click to expand...

Hi Martyn,

The insert was added purely as an "extra", based on MB's replica build (as I don't believe it was on the original model).

As a reference, here is MB's pic that I based it off:

[IMAGE: attachment.php]

Looking at it, I don't think there is any need to extend the sidewalls down to the hull. As you note, we have plenty of stability in the design as it currently stands. If you reduce the height (and angle if required) of the insert side walls (which would essentially raise the "floor"), you then simply glue the insert to the inside face of the hatch panel. 

Of course, not having it on the SU ship means you can make whatever artistic license you choose :lol. 

How's the rest of the build going?

Did you manage to get the missing/duplicate/unfinished pieces sorted out?
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #973  (forum post #2713201)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Jan 26, 2013 at 9:06 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Yep, I do plan to glue it to the inside face of the hatch panel. Hey, we don't have an actual hatch, do we? Wondering whether it's worth CGing one. 

Build's going great! I'm being deliberately sloppy in terms of squaring up and so on so I'm getting small issues here and there. The idea is to anticipate problems on a 'worst case scenario' basis: if I build as badly as I know how, will this still be a stable and presentable model? Because if I do get good results then *nobody* should be able to **** it up. :lol So far so good. 

I found I managed to get an approximately 1mm taper on both engine mount boxes - they flare slightly towards the stern. It's bizarre - both of them are the same, it manifests as toe-out when fitting the rear quarter panels but also toe-in when fitting the hatch assembly. Figure that one out, cos I can't. :lol

It doesn't have any major impact though, hatch assembly can still be jammed in there. I'll be busy tomorrow but I'm nearly ready to start fitting the main hull plates.

Nope, I haven't marked up and cut replacements for the missing bits yet; haven't needed them so far.

Post #998  (forum post #2727469)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Feb 3, 2013 at 9:31 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Cheers, Rod! Was a good yak. 

I just finished up the last main structural stuff at last, for a fast build I really slowed down at the end there. Started sanding and putty today. I have a couple more small mods to do and Simon's bringing a recut version of the mis-cut sheet later this week, since I stuffed up the T5 pieces trying to manually score and snap them out of the sheet like a noob. I've GOT a perfectly good Dremel, arrrgh! (Easy to score and snap 3mm acrylic, but not when it has a transverse .75mm channel cut into it.) 

I've fitted up a few of the plating pieces roughly - only two or three, but they seem okay so far. 

There are a couple of gaps and mismatches that I've managed to build in here and there, and I needed to trim both the rear lower quarter panels slighty. These are all small and easily-fixed issues which are down to me. And I'm kinda chuffed from that - you can throw this thing together with barely any care and still get an acceptable result. The gaps are small enough that I'm feeling no shame in just puttying them.

I'm not gonna call it idiot-proof, I've already broken a couple of pieces after all. :lol But it's the next best thing - if you build around the armature then it squares itself, pretty much. Paul, I'll email you some detailed stuff tomorrow, but I'm happy to sign off on the CNC files.

Every time I look at that pyro on my desk I think of you, Simon - really! Just too damn busy with work, then always knackered to do hard, scary stuff like extending pyro noses of an evening... but I WILL get back in the saddle. 

But this Narc is amazing. I once had my mitts on the original Aliens version of the model, in pretty weird circumstances. In Piccadilly, London, about 15 - 20 years ago there used to be this Aliens experience thing. The punters would get taken to the basement and get chased around by dudes in Alien suits. At the street entrance, they had this tiny prop exhibit, which just sat there for years. You could go in there for free and there'd be nobody, no guard, nothing. They had hypersleep caskets, a couple of suits, a gun or two in tall display cases. On the top of one of the cases, which was a man's height, I saw some object sticking over the edge. Reached up and pulled it out a bit - and **** me, it was a Narcissus studio model. Loads of the styrene panels were warping off it. I thought, '*****, does anyone even want this?' The thing had just been left to rot on top of this display case, unguarded...but I was a good boy and put it back.

Post #1033  (forum post #2787131)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Mar 6, 2013 at 10:13 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I sanded the acrylic, I sanded the top surface of the sheet, I even sanded the bottom surface of the sheet. It sticks okay, not as good as polystyrene I suspect but all right.

Unfortunately it was 0.5mm not 0.75mm. Noticeable difference; looks too thin. I was in denial for quite a while but finally had to give in and mike it; sure enough, too thin. We can get 0.75mm polystyrene ex-East, for some reason the local Mulfords doesn't stock it. Not sure what Simon's plans are tho. 

Two of the engines are good to put in rubber and the other two not far off. Might as well get it done. The replacement nozzle is going to save a lot of work on the 'bad' one - it actually came out better than the first 'good' one. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

I actually found the magnet solution very easy to implement. Aside from stupidly gluing one in place in the reverse orientation of course...a mistake so dumb I HAD to make it. :lol

I've picked up some Barnes TC892 for another job. It's a strong urethane (Shore 80D) intended for electronics potting jobs but casts very cleanly. I'll have a lot left over; think I might use it for the engines. With this I won't need to clay up their insides, they'll be strong enough at the same thickness as the prints. It also tends to foam very slightly, so no shrinkage.

Post #1035  (forum post #2787165)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Mar 6, 2013 at 11:12 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

The underside material is the correct thickness but only scored half-way. It is harder than styrene and with the large mileage of scoring required, I'm finding it is blunting my blades rapidly! 

Oh by the way, I found the best method for cleaning up the 'scurf' from the CNC scoring is to adze it down with a single-edged razor blade. How did you do it? I sanded the top half and found that bits of scurf would keep the paper off the surface around them, or wedge into the grooves. Scraping with the blade removes it entirely in no time at all.

Shapeways - oh no - no such luck. The same order contained parts which had entire pieces missing, for no discernible reason. Oh well. Got all the remaining Narc parts now including the tail details. 

The magnets are quite strong but just about dead right for this application IMO. 10mm x 3mm discs.

Post #1064  (forum post #2799879)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Mar 14, 2013 at 7:52 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Oh god, that cat! :lol

First engine pull. This one's no good - wet night tonight, this one foamed up on me. The mould pulls pretty cleanly though; I'll do the others the same way. (I mean, in terms of orientation for the pour, seam location etc...not 'in rubber' or something.) :lol

Pet peeve time: I swear guys...vac and pressure pots are nice and all but if you don't have one, Don't Panic. Just 1) orient the master for moulding in a way that will let air bubbles in the silicone rise away from the surface of as much of the part as possible, and 2) use a silicone that doesn't cure rapidly - overnight, or at least slowly enough to give the bubbles a chance to do their thing. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 And 3) be sure you've got your pour spout in the best possible location. Turn your master over and over and mock up spouts with clay or whatever you prefer. Ask yourself 'will this bottleneck? Will air get past this undercut as the resin flows in? Can I tilt the mould and get a better pour?' Etc.

I wound up with zero air bubbles anywhere near the surface of the part where I least want them, and when pouring resin the finished mould traps no air; it all comes out of the pour spout. Okay this is a simple shape and I know it isn't rocket science to many of you; it's just a drum that I bang every chance I get. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Post #1126  (forum post #2996513)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Jul 31, 2013 at 11:48 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Talc it and if you still get bubbles, just agitate the resin before it sets. The other parts are SAM2 bits, I moulded an entire kit a few years ago.

Leigh I can't recall the hardness rating for this stuff. It's reasonably firm. I should have moulded the inside as a separate piece because they're a sod to demould due to the taper, but eh, no seam lines this way.

BPV can generate an absolutely freaking unnervingly strong sensation. I haven't had an episode in about six months for which I'm majorly grateful BUT stematil may help a lot and keep in mind that the condition isn't threatening*, as I understand things, so try not to freak out too much.

* obvious disclaimer applies: it turns you into a stumbling, collapsing buffoon. Risk of head injury etc. Take care, don't drive, tackle stairs with assistance, all that.

I'm fairly convinced that there's one truck type kit that is missing and will provide a bunch o parts (yes it is wishful thinking).  Anyway here's the bits I'm looking for.

I'm sceptical. The size and price are tempting but it's an ABS system which just about has to mean finicky calibration and cleaning issues all the damn time. As Lee says, resolution is the big thing. But some of the promo objects on the site look visibly rougher than that, which scares me a good deal. Promo stuff should be as good as they can make it...

Sorry for the late response to this, it took me a little longer to sort the parts map than I'd expected...

I think these are the parts you are looking for.

They're from 8 different kits in all, although you'll already have some of them. With the Ertl truck kits some of the parts are common to several models, so any of them could have been the original donors..... I've indicated that on the map. You'll need to get all of the kits for the Narc anyway though.

Keith

Click to expand...

Lee,

I'm glad you mentioned the Space Shuttle.  I was digging through my boxes to get the shuttle out and had to move my Tamiya 88mm Flak Gun. Just for the fun of it I opened the Flak up - I can never resist a look through that kit - and what should be staring me in the face?.... the part I was looking for in the top left of my picture (attached to the Matilda running gear)!

That was a nice surprise.

The other parts I'm still not sure about. The problem with the Centurion bit you mention is the slope on one side.... the piece in the Narcissus recess seems to be a simple rectangular box. At first I'd thought it was one of the boxes from the Matilda (#C11) but I don't think that's right unfortunately. 

The rail from the 8 Rad is an interesting idea, but it doesn't feel right to me either, mainly because of the amount of trimming and cleanup required to make it fit.

The part(s) where the two truck pipes join are almost high enough to poke out of the bay, so it can't just be the M16 piece with a hole drilled in, that sits too low... there's definitely something else there, but I'm still not sure what.

We'll find them eventually though  
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Keith

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Oh hell no, not if you've already done it - the proper way will be much more fun! I don't even recall why we left it out in the first place. That'll fill the hatch-shaped void in the styrene cutting pattern nicely. :thumbsup

Oh a little bit of good news. Recently unearthed new evidence let me to change the cutting pattern on some kit parts. That in turn confirmed the forward slope of the lower engines which we'd worked out only from photos at first, and the width dim for the central band. Parts fit better and the grown and CNC stuff is confirmed accurate to within a nothingth of a buggerall in those areas. Schweeeeeeet.

Post #1276  (forum post #3050891)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Sep 17, 2013 at 2:37 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I have seen the paint-bespattered Mr. Graver and can verify the truth of this claim. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Guys we're going to do the underside well as a unit casting with as many kit parts as possible moulded in; plantons in two-sided moulds where the undercuts demand it. No nasty compromises I promise.

I hope this is okay with everyone but you still get the perspex parts if you prefer to roll your own. AND I'm hoping to mould the same set of parts on a thinner backing WITHOUT the well walls, for you guys. 

Straw poll: these parts are heavily drilled for whatever reason. I'm guessing there might be people who want them that way, people who want them that way but prefer to drill the parts themselves, and people who want the parts pristine. I'm thinking of moulding the "complete" well as the untouched version, and the "for perspex" thin backing version as the drilled version, since it's "more SS" if that makes sense. Good idea? Stupid anal retentive nonsense? :lol

BTW Simon the moulds I can do but running them I dunno! :eek Might have to rustle up more help for that, we'll see.

Sorry guys I ended up being flat chat all of last week on non-modelling stuff, and most of the weekend too. I've been setting up moulds but haven't been able to pour rubber; that'll change tonight as I have two more ready to go and others just needing an answer from someone on a couple of nitpicky questions (SIMON WHERE ARE YOU LOL).

My own model isn't ready for more kit parts just yet as I still have a lot of puttying and sanding to do, but I hope to get parts to Paul soon - his is ready and begging for parts and should make for some very pretty update pics. I've been busy modelling all the kit parts supplied by Martyn. 

Once modeled, they are test fitted to the 3D model and any adjustments/tweaks are made (if required). 

The physical parts are then test fitted to the prototype for final verification of accuracy. 

Some of the kit pieces modeled so far:

View attachment 264645

My hats off to you guys IDing these parts. 

How you figure out what some of these are from the reference pictures is beyond me!

Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Jan 28, 2014 at 9:38 PM
Reactions : Like — Leigh
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Lee's pics are an excellent guide to what's what with this thing. It's deceptive; you don't realise what a greeblie monster the thing is.

Simon's back in town today and hopefully digging a few more well parts out of his stash for me to dunk into rubber. I've been waiting on the well mould on that and also remembered to seek Paul's input too this time (since he's EXCELLENT at finding my mistakes I thought it made more sense to do that BEFORE I make the mould!!) :lol

Expecting to wrap up my part in this pretty soon; after that we should be able to easily see if we've gone wrong anywhere and make fixes to suit. Then Simon just needs to make the cockpit and/or airlock - if we're doing one - and that'll be about it I guess?

Lee I finally got the Tirpitz bits and patches last week, did I say? Many thanks!!!

Post #1421  (forum post #3239114)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Mar 13, 2014 at 11:34 PM
Reactions : Like — RickDTM, struschie
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Casting engines. Got eight sets done so far but waiting on my supplier to get the resin I prefer (Barnes Procast) back in stock as I don't like the PU4 I've had to use instead, it's a bit less crisp and takes longer for demould. 

Waiting on more parts from Simon before wrapping up the well mould and pouring rubber. He's been back and forth from Queensland and there have been more cyclones. He did drop off several of the missing well parts but not all of them. 

He's working on the cockpit. Several more parts IDs have been made and he says he's getting parts squared up for the consoles, we want good fits here so it is tricky as his model isn't as far along. (Simon, come over and use mine by all means).

Then I decided it needed to go deeper inside, especially if I light it:

[IMAGE: 15518749949_e5bf31bd95_c.jpg]

[IMAGE: 15706198142_37a4005e06_c.jpg]

Will add a few pipes/cables once painted to finish it off.

WIP pics of the decals going on.  Not all are on and this is very much the 'test' version. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Several problems are present, mostly that few pictures of the miniature exist after painting.  The best ones of the underside are from the BluRay.

It also appears to have changed a couple of times during filming that create inconsistencies. 

There's also some decal that were certainly added after it was weathered!

Still, it's starting to look like a spaceship now

Click to expand...

Good stuff. The cockpit is almost ready for casting. Just tidying up a few loose ends. It is accurate to the original where we can see it. Unfortunately with only a few shots of the original interior available there are some Kitparts we just can't see. The good news is that when she is all sealed up you can't see them anyway. So everything you can see throught the cockpit glass from outside is as you would on the original. The other spaces have been left blank so you can either GREEBLIE it up, or I will send out the other pieces of they ever show up.

Post #1508  (forum post #3697748)
Author    : zorg
Date      : Jul 13, 2015 at 4:32 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Nice work lee, what mediums are you using for the weathering?
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #1509  (forum post #3697762)
Author    : Lee S
Date      : Jul 13, 2015 at 4:52 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

There's a little airbrushing here and there, but for the most part it's all hand done with model railway weathering powders.  A medium gray, dark grey, and black.  Takes FOREVER! but it works well.  The front had three passes and the rear one, with some secondary work on the 'mechanical' parts.  Most don't notice but in ALIEN the rear is completely white with no weathering as it was under the cover.  I did that first, and then gave the whole thing another pass so it's more as seen in ALIENS.  Just looks too clean without it.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

JHY said:

			Fantastic model. 

So pleased that this kit will happen. Any idea of the likely price?
		

Click to expand...

Not sure but it won't be cheap if you want to build it like the original. I have toyed around with the idea of two vac formed halves around an aluminium armature for the main body, then styrene panels and resin kitparts. Would make it cheaper and a much quicker build time, but it will be just the acrylic first.

Post #1552  (forum post #4067970)
Author    : jedimaster
Date      : Sep 1, 2016 at 2:45 AM
Reactions : Like — Scott Graham, swpropmaker, moffeaton
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

DARKSIDE72 said:

			My second most favorite all time models! Fantastic guys!
		

Click to expand...

Cheers Jamie. These are just rough castings at the mo. Helped me figure out what I need to cast seperately as plant ons etc. But the layouts good so it can only get better from here. The damn humidity here messes with the Silicon Curing and the resin sets ate a stupid rate. But we are on our way to finishing up. If you don't see a part on these then we couldn't find it or see it clear enough with the limited refs we have. Only for the inside you see here though. The exterior is completely id'd apart from one or two really small parts. Everything you see through the cockpit window and in the refs of the interior is present. I'll post better castings tomorrow.
